data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.0.$attribution-component.0.1.0.$author-image.$attribution-photo"><img class="author-photo" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w133/9fba4f8581986a4cd11ea67e1369ecbadc710e06" alt="Rob Pegoraro" style="width:133px;" data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.0.$attribution-component.0.1.0.$author-image.$attribution-photo.0"></a></div></div></div></div></div></div><div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right col-right" style="width:500px;max-width:500px;" data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.1"><div class="text-body Font-B-1-160" data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.1.$text-body"><div class="body read-more-cut" data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.1.$text-body.0"><div class="pre-cut" data-reactid=".136hdnxu4n4.0.0.0.$Pos-r.$article-inner-container.$inset-container.$grid-template.0.$col-left.$content.$grid-content.0.1.$text-body.0.0"><p><img alt="Why the Cops Hate the New Apple and Google Phones" src="https://s.yimg.com/cd/resizer/2.0/FIT_TO_WIDTH-w500/aa10cde54b45204729ecc86a01c2dd0873d4d891.jpg"></p>  <p><span>The police are upset about Apple and Google&#x2019;s latest smartphone advances.</span></p>  <p>The problem is the encryption in both the iOS&#xA0;8 and Android Lollipop operating systems. It is turned on by default, and there is no master key that Apple or Google can give to investigators, even if they have a warrant.</p>  <p>&#x201C;Unlike our competitors, Apple cannot bypass your passcode and therefore cannot access this data,&#x201D; <a href="https://www.apple.com/privacy/government-information-requests/" target="_blank">Apple brags on its site</a>. &#x201C;So it&#x2019;s not technically feasible for us to respond to government warrants.&#x201D;</p>  <p>Google is not as direct in <a href="http://officialandroid.blogspot.com/2014/10/a-sweet-lollipop-with-kevlar-wrapping.html" target="_blank">its security sales pitch for Android 5.0 Lollipop</a>, shipping on the <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/tech/there-are-big-phones-and-then-there-102401634039.html" target="_blank">Nexus&#xA0;6</a> and (slowly) coming to other devices: &#x201C;Full device encryption occurs at first boot, using a unique key that never leaves the device.&#x201D;</p>  <p>What Apple and Google tout as a feature, police see as a bug, and not the kind they can use to listen in on the bad guys.</p>  <p>&#x201C;Encryption threatens to lead all of us to a very dark place,&#x201D; FBI Director James Comey <a href="http://www.fbi.gov/news/speeches/going-dark-are-technology-privacy-and-public-safety-on-a-collision-course" target="_blank">warned in a speech last month</a>. &#x201C;Justice may be denied because of a locked phone or an encrypted hard drive.&#x201D;</p>  <p><strong>Crypto wars<br></strong>To understand why Comey and others are upset, consider how <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cryptography" target="_blank">cryptography</a> works. Intensely complicated math yields a digital lock that cannot be picked in any reasonable period of time. If you want to see the communication, you either get the password, or you give up.</p>  <p>Digital encryption is at work right now, as you read this: Yahoo Tech (and all Yahoo sites) use encryption that scrambles the data flowing between it and your browser. And your Web-mail service is increasingly likely to <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/tech/explained-how-tls-keeps-your-email-secure-88310223169.html" target="_blank">use encryption</a>, too, so your messages can&#x2019;t be read if they are intercepted.</p>  <p>How iOS&#xA0;8 or Android Lollipop differ from most encryption is where the<em> key</em> goes. Instead of appearing on multiple servers, it&#x2019;s a snowflake of a secret, unique and isolated to one device. It&#x2019;s generated and kept on the device; even the manufacturers cannot get the key to decrypt a phone.</p>  <p>Comey and other law enforcement veterans want Apple and Google to relax the robustness. As former U.S. Attorney General Michael Mukasey <a href="http://www.politico.com/morningcybersecurity/1014/morningcybersecurity15685.html" target="_blank">put it an event in Washington last month</a>: &#x201C;The toothpaste needs to get back in the tube.&#x201D;</p>  <p>What if it isn&#x2019;t put back, and we&#x2019;re in a world where unbreakable crypto is widely available and used?</p>  <p>We don&#x2019;t need to speculate, because that world has existed since the 1990s. Pretty Good Privacy &#x2014; an open-source crypto program the government tried to quash by <a href="http://news.cnet.com/Feds-drop-charges-in-encryption-case/2100-1023_3-201991.html" target="_blank">investigating developer Phil Zimmermann</a> for violating weapons-export laws &#x2014; also doesn&#x2019;t offer any <a href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/compromise-needed-on-smartphone-encryption/2014/10/03/96680bf8-4a77-11e4-891d-713f052086a0_story.html" target="_blank">&#x201C;golden key&#x201D;</a> for the police.</p>  <p>PGP is not the easiest app to set up, but Apple&#x2019;s <a href="http://support.apple.com/en-us/HT4790" target="_blank">FileVault</a> has been in OS&#xA0;X since 2011, while <a href="http://windows.microsoft.com/en-us/windows7/products/features/bitlocker" target="_blank">Microsoft&#x2019;s BitLocker</a> has been in some Windows releases for even longer. And there&#x2019;s no evidence of either <a href="https://www.schneier.com/blog/archives/2012/08/an_analysis_of.html" target="_blank">Apple</a> or <a href="http://mashable.com/2013/09/11/fbi-microsoft-bitlocker-backdoor/" target="_blank">Microsoft</a> having built in back doors that police officers or other agencies can use.</p>  <p><strong>Resorting to other tricks<br></strong>Yet police investigations still catch the bad guys. At one extreme, investigators have used court orders to <a href="http://www.cnet.com/news/feds-use-keylogger-to-thwart-pgp-hushmail/" target="_blank">plant malware on suspects&#x2019; machines to record passwords</a>. At the other, there&#x2019;s traditional police work: <a href="https://firstlook.org/theintercept/" target="_blank">The Intercept&#x2019;s</a> Dan Froomkin and Natasha Vargas-Cooper noted that <a href="https://firstlook.org/theintercept/2014/10/17/draft-two-cases-cited-fbi-dude-dumb-dumb/" target="_blank">encryption had nothing to do with solving three of the four cases Comey cited in his speech</a>.</p>  <p><span>For the law-abiding among us, encryption is a good thing &#x2014; as the FBI notes in </span><a href="http://www.fbi.gov/about-us/investigate/counterintelligence/business-travel-brochure" target="_blank">its advice to business travelers</a><span>. </span><span>But even if you never leave the United States and have no corporate foes, knowing that your data can&#x2019;t be sucked out of your phone or computer should give you comfort.</span></p>  <p>And knowing that there&#x2019;s some back door or master key that can be handed over to a governmental agency, or stolen by a criminal one, should make that comfort vanish. It is a rare vulnerability that stays locked up in one lab; just ask a former National Security Agency contractor who learned much about the agency&#x2019;s surveillance during his time there.</p>  <p>&#x201C;These things get found all the time, and they make a product completely untrustworthy and unreliable,&#x201D; Edward Snowden said via a remote and encrypted video interview at <a href="http://www.rcfp.org/encryptnews" target="_blank">a digital-security workshop for journalists</a>&#xA0;on Nov.&#xA0;7. &#x201C;You&#x2019;ll see a whole bunch of intelligence agencies exploiting the same capability.&#x201D;</p>  <div>   <p><a href="http://johnjay.jjay.cuny.edu/profiles/public_management.aspx?key=%5Bemail%5D=%27awandt@jjay.cuny.edu%27" target="_blank">Adam Wandt</a>, a professor and deputy chair at the John Jay College of Criminal Justice in New York, said the encryption on iOS&#xA0;8 and Android&#xA0;5.0 is harder to crack than past encryption systems &#x2014; in part because of requests from police and courts for better security on their own devices. But could you revise them to hide a secret backup key that only police and courts can access? For now, he said, &#x201C;it&#x2019;s near impossible.&#x201D;</p>   <p>Mukasey&#x2019;s description of the Internet at last month&#x2019;s event also applies to any crypto back door: &#x201C;Like a gun, it doesn&#x2019;t know whether to defend or attack.&#x201D;</p>   <p><strong>Attack the network instead<br></strong>But while device encryption has grown much stronger, the networks that make these devices useful still look woefully weak. On Friday, <a href="http://online.wsj.com/articles/americans-cellphones-targeted-in-secret-u-s-spy-program-1415917533?tesla=y&amp;mg=reno64-wsj" target="_blank">The Wall Street Journal&#x2019;s Devlin Barrett reported</a> that the Justice Department has been flying planes equipped with &#x201C;dirtboxes&#x201D; &#x2014; devices that impersonate cellphone transmitters to snoop on the data sent back and forth.</p>   <p>The idea here is to zero in on the phones of suspects and ignore those of others (we must take the DoJ at its word there). Police can already do that by using <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/IMSI-catcher" target="_blank">&#x201C;IMSI catchers&#x201D;</a> to spoof cell towers, but a Cessna above a city will capture far more chatter. And we had no idea this aerial surveillance was going on until a few days ago.</p>   <p>Meanwhile, all the data that&#x2019;s automatically synced from our phones to cloud storage can be <a href="https://www.yahoo.com/tech/be-angry-about-the-icloud-hack-but-not-surprised-96459530239.html" target="_blank">vulnerable to low-grade hacking and compromise</a>, to say nothing of NSA-level prying.</p>   <p>Companies like Apple and Google will make a big mistake if they pat themselves on the back for making encryption the default on a new device and don&#x2019;t keep working just as hard to secure the network services that give those gadgets life.</p>   <p>Meanwhile, the law enforcement advocates angry at Apple and Google for frustrating their jobs should take a moment to think about how their requests look after all these revelations of widespread and industrialized surveillance of networks. Asking tech companies to break their products, even as strong crypto remains a reality elsewhere, is not an argument they can win or should win.</p>   <p><em>Email </em><a href="http://robpegoraro.com/" target="_blank"><span><em>Rob</em></span></a><em> at </em><a href="mailto:rob@robpegoraro.com" target="_blank"><span><em>rob@robpegoraro.com</em></span></a><em>; follow him on Twitter at </em><a href="http://twitter.com/robpegoraro" target="_blank"><span><em>@robpegoraro</em></span></a><em>.</em></p>  </div></div><div class="post-cut" When Burstein searched Twitter, it no longer turned up.","body":"\u003Cdiv\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fe37e1ec3260f7aba00217bea216481f60d4f8ff2.jpg\" alt=\"Twitter Now Lets You Search for Any Tweet Ever Sent\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EPaul Burstein was trying to fix a software bug, and Twitter was helping him out.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThe year was 2011. Burstein worked as an engineer at&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002FSalesforce.com\"\u003Ethe massive internet company Salesforce.com,\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;and&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.exploringbinary.com\u002Fjava-hangs-when-converting-2-2250738585072012e-308\u002F\"\u003Ethe bug\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;a rather annoying flaw in the popular&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2013\u002F09\u002Fthe-second-coming-of-java\u002Fall\u002F\"\u003EJava programming tools\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;was causing problems with the company&#x2019;s online services. He&#x2019;d learned of the bug when someone tweeted out a webpage describing the thing, and each time he needed to re-check the details, he would search Twitter, find that tweet, and return to the webpage.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIt&#x2019;s the sort of thing people so often do as they look for stuff they&#x2019;ve previously visited online. But then, after about a week, that tweet disappeared. When Burstein searched Twitter, it no longer turned up.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThis was the way things were supposed to work. Originally, Twitter built its search engine to provide quick access to what people are tweeting right now&#x2014;not to what they&#x2019;ve tweeted in the past&#x2014;and that meant removing&#xA0;\u003Cspan\u003Eevery tweet\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E&#xA0;from its search index after a week or so. But Burstein also knew this wasn&#x2019;t ideal. It&#x2019;s one of the reasons he soon left Salesforce for a job at Twitter. &#x201C;I felt like there were interesting search problems to be solved,&#x201D; he says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002Fon-learning-by-doing\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003EAmerican Schools Are Training Kids for a World That Doesn&#x2019;t Exist\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIndeed there were. Shortly after he arrived at Twitter, Burstein and a small team of other engineers started work on a new search engine that could quickly comb through not only the millions of tweets sent over the past several of days, but also the hundreds of billions of tweets sent since the service first launched in 2006. Along the way, they rolled out preliminary versions of this tool that could search parts of its massive archive&#x2014;the first in 2012, another last year&#x2014;and now, the project is complete.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThis morning, Twitter&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblog.twitter.com\u002F2014\u002Fbuilding-a-complete-tweet-index\"\u003Ebegan rolling out\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;a search service that lets you search for any tweet in its archive.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EOutside services have long offered ways of searching old tweets, including tools like&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftopsy.com\u002F\"\u003ETopsy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;(\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fonline.wsj.com\u002Farticles\u002FSB10001424052702304854804579234450633315742\"\u003Enow owned by Apple)\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;and&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.twimemachine.com\u002F\"\u003ETweet Machine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and such services are still the best way to find tweets that have been&#xA0;\u003Cspan\u003Edeleted\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E&#xA0;from Twitter proper. But Twitter&#x2019;s new search engine fills a conspicuous hole in its own micro-messaging service, and shows how internet search services continue to evolve, providing ever faster access to an ever growing corpus of online information.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThough the new Twitter search engine is limited to rather rudimentary keyword searches today, the company plans to expand into more complex queries in the months and years to come. And the foundational search infrastructure laid down by the company will help drive other Twitter tools as well. &#x201C;It lets us power a lot more things down the road&#x2014;not just search,&#x201D; says Gilad Mishne, the Twitter engineering director who helped oversee the project.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EFrom the First Tweet to the Last\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EMishne recently demonstrated the new search engine during a gathering of Twitter employees at the company&#x2019;s headquarters in San Francisco. The money moment was when he showed that Twitter search now lets you find the first ever tweet: founder Jack Dorsey&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftwitter.com\u002Fjack\u002Fstatuses\u002F20\"\u003Etelling the world\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;he&#x2019;s &#x201C;just setting up my twttr.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThat tweet isn&#x2019;t that hard find through Google and other web search engines, simply because it&#x2019;s been cited so often. But the new Twitter search can just as readily find Dorsey&#x2019;s second tweet and his third and so on&#x2014;all the way up to tweets sent in the last few minutes.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002F21-awesomely-well-designed-products-dying\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003E21 Awesomely Well-Designed Products We&#x2019;re Dying to Own\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIt may seem perplexing that Twitter didn&#x2019;t offer such a search engine long ago. But Twitter did not even have a search engine for recent tweets until 2011, five years after the company was founded. Though it handles enormous amounts of online traffic&#x2014;the microblogging service now boasts 284 million users&#x2014;the company&#x2019;s engineering team is still relatively small, and it tends to expand its online tools at a rather gradual pace.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EBuilding an all-encompassing search is rather difficult&#x2014;and quite different from fashioning a tool that searches recent tweets. As Mishne puts it, the company&#x2019;s first order of business was to provide a window into what&#x2019;s happening now. &#x201C;We&#x2019;re a realtime platform. This is what Twitter is,&#x201D; he says. &#x201C;So we focused first on solving the realtime search problem.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EBeyond Memory\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIts original realtime search engine was based on what&#x2019;s called an &#x201C;in-memory&#x201D; system. Basically, in order to provide quick access to tweets, the company stored them in the main memory subsystems of a vast network of computers&#x2014;as opposed to on hard disks, which read and write data at much slower rates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EBut it was too expensive and, at least in the short-term, too difficult to set up enough machines to store all tweets in memory. So, after several days, the company would drop tweets out of its index and store them elsewhere. &#x201C;We had to make a tradeoff&#x2014;do things as soon as possible while trading off the depth of the index,&#x201D; Burstein says.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThis worked well enough, as the system could store a few billion tweets in memory, but Burstein and company knew the search engine needed to do more. As has so often been the case with other Twitter tools, the company had spent years standing back as third parties built search engines that could search for older tweets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ESome of these worked pretty well, with Twitter providing them with direct access to its &#x201C;firehose&#x201D; of tweets. But they didn&#x2019;t necessarily provide instant access to brand new tweets. They didn&#x2019;t tightly integrate with Twitter itself. And they&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Ftweetscan.com\u002F\"\u003Edidn&#x2019;t always last.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;So, in late 2011, Burstein and few others, including engineer Yi Zhuang, went to work on a search engine that would directly tap the Twitter archive.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003E&#x2018;Can We Really Do This?&#x2019;\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ETo hear Burstein tell it, this wasn&#x2019;t an easy thing. &#x201C;When we started,&#x201D; he remembers, &#x201C;I would frequently come into the office and say: &#x2018;can we really do this?&#x2019;&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIt wasn&#x2019;t just that they needed to index every tweet in existence. They needed to find a way of constantly merging this index with the millions of new tweets that go out with each passing second. This, says Mike Miller,&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F05\u002Fcloud-service-as-m-and-a-tool\u002F\"\u003Ethe CTO of online database outfit Cloudant\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which has worked with outside companies on Twitter search engines, is the really difficult part.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EWhen Twitter and other realtime services rose to prominence several years ago, Google refashioned its search engine so that it could handle the most resent of internet posts alongside much older data, and this required a&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theregister.co.uk\u002F2009\u002F08\u002F14\u002Fgoogle_caffeine_truth\u002F\"\u003Emassive overhaul\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;of the sweeping software systems that drive its search engine. Now, Twitter has done much the same.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fwet-dogs\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003EAdorable Photos of Emotional, Wet Dogs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EBasically, Burstein and crew use hundreds of machines running Hadoop MapReduce&#x2014;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002Ftwitter-now-lets-search-tweet-ever-sent\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2011\u002F10\u002Fhow-yahoo-spawned-hadoop\u002Fall\u002F\"\u003Ethe popular open source data-crunching tool\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#x2014;to collect and arrange all the data needed for its master search index, and then they use separate custom-built software to actually build the index. The trick is that a relatively small number of machines builds each part of the index. &#x201C;We can massively parallelize the process,&#x201D; says Burstein.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIn short, one group of machines can build a portion of the index for older tweets while another is building a portion for newer tweets. The same basic software that handles the archive can also handle the realtime stuff.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EFlash to the Future\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThe system can still do all this at speed&#x2014;but it doesn&#x2019;t try to stuff everything in memory. Instead, it uses machines equipped with solid-state disks, or SSDs. Basically, these are&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2012\u002F06\u002Fflash-data-centers\u002F\"\u003Emodern replacements for hard disks\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, built from flash memory, the same stuff that stories data and applications on your smartphone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EReading and writing data on SSDs is significantly faster than juggling information on hard disks, and SSDs aren&#x2019;t quite as expensive as storing data in main memory. This is part of a larger shift in the world of computing, with so many large operations aiming to provide&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002Ftwitter-now-lets-search-tweet-ever-sent\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2012\u002F06\u002Fflash-data-centers\u002Fall\u002F\"\u003Equicker access to more online data\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. In Twitter, you can see a reflection of the internet as a whole.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Cimg src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" Them\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E*&#xA0;\u003Ca Aren&#x2019;t Using It\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E*&#xA0;\u003Ca Official—iOS 8 Is Apple’s Buggiest Release to Date","summary":"When Apple first released the iPhone 6, we were struck by the surprisingly persistent and numerous bugs in iOS 8.  Almost all review units (from any company, not just Apple) are thoroughly tested, vetted, and hand-selected as being the best representation of that product.  So using an iPhone that rebooted itself and got hung up on the keyboard was surprising indeed.  WIRED saw similar bugs on the iPhone 6 Plus.Other reviewers pronounced it Apple’s buggiest release yet, and Apple pundit John Gruber wrote “it seems like Apple’s software teams can’t keep up with the pace of the hardware teams” before talking more about getting stuck in an endless reboot cycle.","body":"\u003Cdiv\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"It&#x2019;s Official&#x2014;iOS 8 Is Apple&#x2019;s Buggiest Release to Date\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F8aa10964137751350448db370e3e61d28fdf3ba8.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EWhen Apple first released the iPhone 6,&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fiphone-6-review\u002F\"\u003Ewe were struck\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;by the surprisingly persistent and numerous bugs in iOS 8. Almost all review units (from any company, not just Apple) are thoroughly tested, vetted, and hand-selected as being the best representation of that product. You don&#x2019;t want a reviewer accidentally ending up with a blemished, defective phone. Bad publicity. So using an iPhone that rebooted itself and got hung up on the keyboard was surprising indeed.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EWe weren&#x2019;t alone in that sentiment. WIRED saw&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fiphone-6-plus-review\u002F\"\u003Esimilar bugs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;on the iPhone 6 Plus.\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2014\u002F9\u002F23\u002F6826561\u002Fios-8-review\"\u003EOther reviewers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;pronounced it Apple&#x2019;s buggiest release yet, and Apple pundit John Gruber wrote &#x201C;it seems like Apple&#x2019;s software teams can&#x2019;t keep up with the pace of the hardware teams&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fdaringfireball.net\u002Flinked\u002F2014\u002F10\u002F01\u002Fit-just-works\"\u003Ebefore talking more\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;about getting stuck in an endless reboot cycle.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F10\u002Fon-learning-by-doing\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003EAmerican Schools Are Training Kids for a World That Doesn&#x2019;t Exist\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ETurns out it wasn&#x2019;t just in our heads: Data from app performance monitor\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.crittercism.com\u002Fios-8-performance\u002F\"\u003ECrittercism\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;showed iOS 8&#x2019;s crash rate was 60 percent higher than iOS 7 during their respective first months on handsets.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I find myself at once impressed by the overall quality of iOS, and surprised by the seemingly obvious problems that have recently made it past QA,&#x201D; Red Sweater Software founder and ex-Apple software quality engineer Daniel Jalkut told WIRED via email about iOS 8. Jalkut shed some light on how bugs can slip through:\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cblockquote\u003E \n  \u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Some bugs, like the HealthKit problems that botched iOS 8.0&#x2019;s debut, and the problems with 8.0.1, were clearly issues that Apple had not identified, or they would have found a way to fix them before releasing. Other, less dramatic issues could really come down to a manager at Apple being hard-pressed to meet a deadline and &#x201C;punting&#x201D; (that&#x2019;s a common term used in reviewing bugs at Apple) the problems down to the next release, or even later.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003C\u002Fblockquote\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThis is something that obviously happens with every major software release. But with iOS 8 more slipped by than in any other iOS version before it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EThe Reports\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ELooking at past bug reports seemed like a good way to better understand whether iOS 8 was actually &#x201C;buggier.&#x201D; Anecdotally, it&#x2019;s difficult to quantify how many bugs each iOS version has. There are&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fforums.macrumors.com\u002Fshowthread.php?t=1784503\"\u003Eforum threads\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;upon&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fforums.macrumors.com\u002Fshowthread.php?t=1621922\"\u003Eforum threads\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.iphonehacks.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fios-8-bugs.html\"\u003Eposts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;upon\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.macworld.com\u002Farticle\u002F2010812\u002Fbugs-and-fixes-troubleshooting-ios-6.html\"\u003Eposts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;outlining all the issues iOS users have experienced through the years. Some affect hundreds or thousands of users, others, less than a dozen (Take, for example,\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fiphone-6-plus-bendgate\u002F\"\u003EBendgate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E: Despite wide publicity, the issue only affected a small number of iPhone 6 Plus owners).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We expect perfection, and when we don&#x2019;t get it, we tell the world,&#x201D; Matt Johnston, chief strategy officer at app testing and analytics firm Applause, told WIRED. Everyone is holding a digital megaphone thanks to social media. &#x201C;Even the best software companies stumble, and when they do, users will air their dissatisfaction far and wide.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EAnd knowing, from reports and forum discussions, that the bugs experienced by an iPhone owner can very dramatically from handset to handset, we couldn&#x2019;t just go off our personal OS issues, either.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002F21-awesomely-well-designed-products-dying\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003E21 Awesomely Well-Designed Products We&#x2019;re Dying to Own\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ESo we turned to Apple&#x2019;s official Support pages on iOS updates for an objective perspective on iOS bug fixes. These outline the additions and bug fixes for each version (like&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fsupport.apple.com\u002Fkb\u002FDL1758\"\u003Ethis one\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;for iOS 8.0.2 or&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fsupport.apple.com\u002Fkb\u002FDL1606\"\u003Ethis one\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;for iOS 6.0.1). Counting items that were clearly bug fixes or improvements that resolved issues (rather than ones that added a new functionality or feature) as a metric, iOS 8, to start with at least, wasn&#x2019;t all that different from past launches.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EIt had the same number of bugs as the launch of iOS 6: 8 issues fixed in the .0.1 update (which was quickly pulled in the case of iOS 8), and one more tacked on in the .0.2 update. Fewer bugs were addressed initially in iOS 7, but it had 8 to 9 bug fixes in its late October 2013&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fsupport.apple.com\u002Fkb\u002FDL1691\"\u003E7.0.3\u003C\u002Fa\u003E&#xA0;update. Over the course of their whole existence, iOS 6 had approximately 21 total bug fixes, while in iOS 7, that number climbed slightly to 27.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EChronologically, these updates are coming faster and faster. If you look at the timeline for Apple&#x2019;s iOS updates, some general trends start to emerge: Apple is rolling out updates to iOS a lot quicker after the initial OS launch. For example, the first OS update to iOS 5 was about a month after launch; the first to iOS 6, a month and a half later; while iOS 7 had four updates from its September 18 debut through mid-November. More bugs are being addressed through these updates.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EAbout a month and a half into iOS 8: We&#x2019;ve had four updates (8.0.1, 8.0.2. 8.1, and 8.1.1), and we&#x2019;re officially at 23 listed bug fixes through iOS 8.1. But with iOS 8.1.1, which just went live Monday, Apple doesn&#x2019;t site specific bug fixes, but rather a general &#x201C;This release includes bug fixes, increased stability and performance improvements for iPad 2 and iPhone 4s.&#x201D; It&#x2019;s not a leap to assume that &#x201C;bug fixes,&#x201D; plural, refers to at least two to three fixes, and that stability updates to older iOS devices could bring that number to at least five. That officially makes iOS 8, thus far, the buggiest iOS yet.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EA Fuller Picture\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EObviously, straight numbers don&#x2019;t paint a complete picture of what&#x2019;s going on.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EAt the same time that bug numbers are rising, iOS has grown&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002Fios-8-buggiest\u002F\"\u003Einto its most complex, advanced iteration yet\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and Apple&#x2019;s vastly expanded its hardware offerings, too. Instead of a singular iPhone on one carrier, Apple now sells four iPhone models and supports six; sells five iPad models and supports eight; and it sells the fifth-generation iPod touch, too. On top of that, the iPhone and iPad are available on hundreds of different carriers worldwide. That in itself is good reason why there could be more bugs Apple has to fix in iOS 8 than in the past.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fwet-dogs\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003EAdorable Photos of Emotional, Wet Dogs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EBut there are other factors too. Starting with the fourth generation iPad (the first with Retina display) and iPad mini, Apple switched the iPad launch date to late fall, following its annual iPhone launch. With this change, it makes sense that the past few years would show a quicker rollout of bug fixes towards the beginning of the iOS life cycle, as iOS may have to be updated to support new hardware models.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EApple could also simply be addressing more bugs than it was able to in the past, fixing smaller issues that affect fewer people, rather than only&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2010\u002F07\u002Fiphone-4\u002F\"\u003EAntennagate\u003C\u002Fa\u003E-level woes. Apple&#x2019;s Support pages don&#x2019;t say how many people are affected by each bug fix.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EHowever, with an increasingly complex OS and hardware, it doesn&#x2019;t help the bug issue by launching both at the same time each year.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Ch3\u003EThe Price of Fast-Paced Hardware\u002FSoftware Releases\u003C\u002Fh3\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EThrowing new hardware and software out at the same time, as Apple does with iOS and iPhone launches, is potentially great for users and sales, but adds more variables to the mix for developers and testers who have to make stuff &#x201C;just work,&#x201D; Johnston says. Some have posited that if Apple slowed up its yearly production cycle, unbundling the launch of a big new OS with a big new piece of hardware, Apple could do a better job of preventing bugs from sneaking into final builds. But that could impact Apple&#x2019;s competitiveness in the fast-paced mobile market.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I see [Apple&#x2019;s] challenge as one in which they have to try to balance striving for utmost quality with the fact that competitors are coming up with new phones and OS updates that threaten to upend Apple&#x2019;s relatively strong position,&#x201D; Jalkut said.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003ESlowing its product cycle could also impact Apple&#x2019;s already fragile perception as a\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2013\u002F09\u002Fapple-annoucements\u002F\"\u003Eleader of innovation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. With this in mind, and all those investors to please, it seems unlikely Apple would do that.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EREAD:&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002Fmicronations\u002F?mbid=synd_yahootech\"\u003EThe World&#x2019;s Tiniest Countries and the Eccentrics Who Rule Them\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n \u003Cp\u003EAnd so Apple&#x2019;s entwined itself in a production cycle that includes shipping with some known bugs and addressing them rapid fire in subsequent platform updates. We are, it would seem, seeing more bugs in iOS than we used to&#x2014;at least at the outset. With our expectations rising, the richness and complexity of iOS growing at an exponential rate, and&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.wired.com\u002F2014\u002F09\u002Fapples-new-wearable\u002F\"\u003Ea completely new form factor on the horizon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it&#x2019;s going to be a tough trend to reverse. Perhaps in iOS 9, Apple will be able to reel in more bugs before they hit user&#x2019;s devices. Normally we don&#x2019;t share those with you here on Yahoo Tech.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBut the (cough) innovations that emerged from a hackathon this past weekend are \u003Cem\u003Esupposed \u003C\u002Fem\u003Eto be stupid &#x2014; that&#x2019;s why it&#x2019;s called the \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fstupidhackathon.com\"\u003EStupid S*** No One Needs &amp; Terrible Ideas Hackathon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ENormally, a hackathon (or hack day, or similar) is a limited-time event that supposedly squeezes fresh creativity out of code-jockeys who have to come up with \u003Cem\u003Esomething\u003C\u002Fem\u003E in, say, 24 hours. It&#x2019;s a particularly trendy maneuver among tech firms that revel in a cutting-edge, try-something-new mentality as a path to true innovation.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis hackathon is different. Organized by \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flav.io\u002F\"\u003ESam Lavigne\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.studioamelia.com\u002F\"\u003EAmelia Winger-Bearskin\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it&#x2019;s an event that specifically &#x201C;asks participants to produce projects that have no value whatsoever.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EStill, the people who participate are actually quite talented and clever, and of course the real point of the event is to produce ideas that are stupid in interesting, amusing, and maybe perversely insightful ways.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EBelow, a few favorites.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E(All images and videos via the full rundown at Lavigne&#x2019;s site, which you can peruse \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flav.io\u002F2014\u002F11\u002Fstupid-projects-from-the-stupid-hackathon\u002F\"\u003Ehere\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. (Alyssa Bereznak\u002FYahoo Tech)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOn Tuesday, the French drone company Parrot released its latest flying machine, the Bebop drone. The Bebop &#x2014; so named for its ability to &#x201C;dance&#x201D; in the air &#x2014; \u003C\u002Fspan\u003Eis equipped with a high-definition 14-megapixel camera, which is held stable with the help of shock-absorbing pads, and comes with an optional joystick-like controller to make flying easier for beginners.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EBebop pilots can move the camera&#x2019;s view separately from the machine, within a 180-degree field. It can be controlled from either your tablet or a separate navigation tool called the Skycontroller.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThis should mean more majestic and high-definition drone-shot wedding videos in the near future.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Parrot Bebop drone\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F3516b032c27ec3f61fd8e79fb34f7f61b837d0e5.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Bebop avoids shaky footage in a number of ways through software that fixes the angle of the drone&#x2019;s shots, smoothing over jagged takes, and through internal chips that digitally enhance what you&#x2019;ve recorded.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"GIF showing Parrot Bebop drone in flight\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002Foriginal\u002Flb2XKfyYW2YQxDSqy-R20hZ0j0I.gif\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EWhile the Bebop&#x2019;s sensors allow it to be controlled via Wi-Fi from any Android or iOS operating system, it can also be paired with a new accessory to help with the operation. The Skycontroller, which is reminiscent of a gaming controller you might play with at an arcade, can be fitted onto your tablet to create a centralized navigation center.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Parrot Bebop drone&apos;s Skycontroller\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F905adde8101cb97a93524805df700f01fef275a2.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003EThe Skycontroller. (Alyssa Bereznak\u002FYahoo Tech)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou simply throw a strap over your neck like you would with a camera and position your hands on two joysticks. A panel above your tablet is equipped with antennas that extend the reach of your Wi-Fi connection, so that you can terrorize your neighbors from as far as 1.2 miles away. The contraption is meant to help inexperienced fliers become accustomed to drone basics, with easy-to use launch, recording, and emergency landing buttons. I had tried flying a drone only once before but was able to easily navigate a Bebop through an open studio.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe only downside? Depending on what you&#x2019;re doing with the drone, and whether you&#x2019;re flying it with its detachable foam protectors, each battery gives you only 10 minutes of flying time. It comes with two, but they take about an hour and 45 minutes to charge.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn other words, you can creep on people only in short spurts. Also, that would have to be a pretty quick wedding!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Parrot Bebop drone starts at $500 and will be available in December for $500. You can buy it with the Skycontroller for $900, if you&#x2019;re extra fancy. Is Nokia’s Comeback Device (Look Familiar?)","summary":"Nokia's new N1 is an Android-powered tablet that's a dead ringer for Apple's iPad mini.","body":"\u003Cdiv\u003E \n \u003Cdiv\u003E \n  \u003Cdiv\u003E\n   \u003Cimg alt=\"This Is Nokia&#x2019;s Comeback Device (Look Familiar?)\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F3fc8157763709a3a7e58132f5e22506be1eca42a.jpg\"\u003E\n   \u003Cbr\u003E\n   \u003Cem\u003E(Reuters)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\n  \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n  \u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n  \u003Cdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \n  \u003Cdiv\u003E\n   Love the way Apple&#x2019;s iPad mini looks, but can&#x2019;t cut ties with Google&#x2019;s Android operating system? Well, Nokia&#x2019;s new N1 tablet just might be the one for you. Unveiled today, the \n   \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fn1.nokia.com\u002F\"\u003ENokia N1\u003C\u002Fa\u003E tablet runs Android while also looking so much like Apple&#x2019;s iPad mini that you might not be able to tell a difference at first glance. \n   \u003Cp\u003EThe first device to come from Nokia since its phone division was purchased by Microsoft, the N1 is a 7.9-inch tablet with a display resolution of 2048 &#xD7; 1536, like the iPad mini, and features an aluminum body, also like the mini. The N1&#x2019;s speakers look similar to the mini&#x2019;s. Heck, even the N1&#x2019;s volume and power buttons are in the same place as the mini&#x2019;s.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003EMeasuring 7.9 &#xD7; 5.5 &#xD7; 0.27 inches and weighing 0.7 pounds, the N1 is a bit wider but still slimmer than Apple&#x2019;s iPad mini. The N1 weighs a drop less than the mini, 0.7 pounds vs. 0.73 pounds.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F9dece67c50d5f682756a3175f6b9ee6c4dede2f6.png\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOK, so it looks like an iPad mini, but what can the N1 offer that the iPad can&#x2019;t? Well, the N1 comes loaded with Google&#x2019;s new Android&#xA0;5.0 Lollipop operating system. Riding on top of that is Nokia&#x2019;s new Z Launcher, an Android &#x201C;skin&#x201D; in the same vein as Samsung&#x2019;s TouchWiz and HTC&#x2019;s Sense interfaces.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003EZ Launcher looks and feels completely different from the standard Android Lollipop operating system, but it still runs the same apps and has the same basic settings menus. What sets Z Launcher apart from other Android skins is how you interact with it.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003EWhile on the home screen, you can write the first letter of the app you want to open, and Z Launcher will automatically search for it for you. What&#x2019;s more, the interface learns which apps you use the most and at what time and ensures that they are on the home screen when you&#x2019;re likely to need them.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Nokia N1 Android tablet\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fca3cfbf2bdd877c50ec392b52b11002c35141f90.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EUnlike the iPad mini, the N1 gets an 8-megapixel rear camera and a 5-megapixel front camera. (The mini features a 5-megapixel iSight rear camera and a 1.2-megapixel FaceTime front camera.)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003EAs a bonus, the N1 comes with a reversible USB Type-C port, which means you don&#x2019;t have to struggle while trying to plug in a microUSB port the right way. A new kind of connection, the reversible micro-USB port lets you insert your charging cord either way, so that it&#x2019;s never &#x201C;upside-down.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003ESo when can you get the Nokia N1? According to the company, the tablet will launch in China in time for the first quarter of 2015 for about $249. That&#x2019;s well below the $399 the iPad mini&#xA0;3 costs and the $299 the mini&#xA0;2 goes for.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ERelease dates for the U.S. haven&#x2019;t been revealed, but Nokia said it anticipates selling the tablet in the rest of the world sometime after its Chinese launch date.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n   \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EWe&#x2019;ll get our hands on an N1 to give you a better idea of how it looks and feels in the near future. He refused to comment on a \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002FptRTvxHlPE\u002F?modal=true\"\u003Ephoto of my cat\u003C\u002Fa\u003E I&#x2019;d been quite proud of and said my \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002FNRpExnHlKa\u002F?modal=true\"\u003Ephoto of the Santa Monica Pier\u003C\u002Fa\u003E was boring (which is fair).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EInstead, he said, &#x201C;I\u003Cspan\u003E&#xA0;just started scrolling through to see what caught my eye.&#x201D; His commentary is below.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"580.0653594771242\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002Fh0MAR\u002Fembed\u002F\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E&#x201C;If it was a perfect picture, the guy underneath the hooves wouldn&#x2019;t have been there, but that&#x2019;s just the way it goes. It has nothing to do with the way you shot it or anything, it&#x2019;s just that there&#x2019;s a person on both sides of the horse&#x2019;s hooves, but then there&#x2019;s one that&#x2019;s right below it. If that person wasn&#x2019;t there, it would just really make it a better picture. you wouldn&#x2019;t have been so distracted. What I like about it is the movement up and down. This is kind of reminiscent of a [\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EHenri] Cartier-Bresson\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E picture, where you have all these people but they&#x2019;re separated out. It&#x2019;s a good picture, but it could&#x2019;ve been great if all those circumstances would&#x2019;ve fallen into place. I could see greatness there, an almost Diane Arbus flare to it. But that&#x2019;s not complementing the people necessarily.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"580.0653594771242\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002FebCbpVnlKz\u002Fembed\u002F\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E&#x201C;This photo cries for black-and-white.&#xA0;The picture isn&#x2019;t bad, it&#x2019;s just a situation where you really should have worked it more. I like the white hat in the foreground, that&#x2019;s great. The balloons, too. It seemed like a different era, almost a \u003Cem\u003EGreat Gatsby\u003C\u002Fem\u003E thing. Part of my suggestion to you would be to shoot more pictures, because you&#x2019;re on to something in the first place. You should&#x2019;ve tried angles lower or higher, or focus on the quality. When you shoot at a crowd, it&#x2019;s hard with the iPhone. You always need to look for a point of interest&#x2014;a face in the crowd, something that&#x2019;s not related to what&#x2019;s going on. That makes the picture more interesting.&#x201D;&#xA0;\u003Ciframe height=\"580.0653594771242\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002FsxEuFAHlEL\u002Fembed\u002F\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E&#x201C;\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThis is one of your best pictures. The cat is displaying its personality. Everything about it works. If I had to [pick one], this is the one I like best.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"580.0653594771242\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Finstagram.com\u002Fp\u002FckNcvXHlBM\u002Fembed\u002F\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E&#x201C;This is really nice. Obviously, it&#x2019;s thanks to the artist [James Turrell], but your interpretation of it is very nice. The concentric lines coming out and the vividness of the color that just pops out at you. This is one where you can take it in Photoshop and boost the contrast a little bit. In my\u003Cspan\u003E&#xA0;book I talk about shooting in museums. You&#x2019;re interpreting other people&#x2019;s art, or your interpreting other people&#x2019;s interpretations of art. Announces Snapcash, a Way to Send Money to Friends","summary":"Mobile messaging company Snapchat is launching a new service that lets users send money to one another, in a partnership with online payments company Square. The service, dubbed Snapcash, allows Snapchat users to link their debit cards to their accounts and quickly send money to a contact by starting a chat on a smartphone, typing in a dollar sign and an amount and hitting a green button, Snapchat explained in a post on its official blog Monday.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Snapchat Announces Snapcash, a Way to Send Money to Friends\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fe4fe160a2ec0a9464ebf9803b98a8aa31f90118e.png\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(Snapchat\u002FYouTube)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EMobile messaging company Snapchat is launching a new service that lets users send money to one another, in a partnership with online payments company Square.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe service, dubbed Snapcash, allows Snapchat users to link their debit cards to their accounts and quickly send money to a contact by starting a chat on a smartphone, typing in a dollar sign and an amount and hitting a green button, Snapchat explained in a post on its official blog Monday.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe move marks the latest sign of expansion plans for Los Angeles-based Snapchat, which lets users exchange photos that automatically disappear after a few seconds. The company has been valued at $10 billion in its most recent fundraising effort, according to media reports, and is considered a growing threat to Web companies including Facebook and Twitter.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;We set out to make payments faster and more fun, but we also know that security is essential when you&#x2019;re dealing with money,&#x201D; Snapchat said in the post.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe company said that debit card information will be stored by Square and that Square will process the payments, transferring money between bank accounts. Snapchat said Snapcash is available in the United States for users age 18 and above.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ELast month Snapchat began showing ads on its service for the first T-Mobile UK (a differently owned and operated company from T-Mobile in the United States) for a contract plan. sapphire touchscreen display. It'll be available in December for $495 at Opening Ceremony’s online and retail stores and at Barney’s.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Intel&#x2019;s New Luxury Smart Bracelet, MICA, Will Offer Texting and Alerts\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F3bb3b4310d9f503c3c0b1dbec8be4805e2962d4c.png\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe MICA bracelet. (Intel)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cem\u003EBrace\u003C\u002Fem\u003E yourselves: Your jewelry is about to get its own apps.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EIn a joint presentation on Monday, computing giant Intel and New York-based fashion retailer Opening Ceremony revealed the features and final form of their new bracelet, the MICA. Short for &#x201C;My Intelligent Communication Accessory,&#x201D; the bracelet will allow you to access text messages, Gmail, Yelp, GPS, and Google and Facebook events. The device, which features a curved sapphire touchscreen display, will be available in December for $495 at Opening Ceremony&#x2019;s online and retail stores and at Barney&#x2019;s.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"MICA smart bracelet\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F287604f447f065bcd69c19b40b1d31bde91bb432.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E(Alyssa Bereznak\u002FYahoo Tech)\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EUnlike other wristwatch computers, such as the Apple Watch and several devices running Google&#x2019;s Android Wear, MICA does not have to be connected to a smartphone to operate. Instead, similar to&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Fwill-i-am-launches-a-smartwatch-puls-which-he-calls-100165104289.html\"\u003EWil.i.am&#x2019;s Puls smart cuff\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, it&#x2019;ll be powered by its own two-year AT&amp;T data contract, &#x201C;paid for by Intel,&#x201D; after which \u003Cspan\u003EIntel Vice President Ayse&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003EIldeniz says you and AT&amp;T will have to &#x201C;re-contract.&#x201D; (Asked what that means, she admitted that the company hadn&#x2019;t worked out what exactly that would do to the wallets of MICA owners.)\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe bangle, which was first announced during Fashion Week this past September, is made in two colors: black and white. Both have an 18-carat gold coating. One comes with black water snake skin, Chinese pearls, and lapis stones from Madagascar. The other is made from white water snake skin, tiger&#x2019;s eye from South Africa, and obsidian from Russia. When I tried one on during a quick hands-on demo, it was light on the wrist, fit well, and was comfortable to wear.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Black MICA smart bracelet\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Faffb5b157e27f95b225e1589d438c599aade8797.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe MICA bracelet in black. \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E(Alyssa Bereznak\u002FYahoo Tech)\u003Cspan\u003E&#xA0;\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003ERather than carry a display at the top of the bracelet, MICA is designed for women to glance at and swipe notifications from the insides of their wrists. These include something Intel calls &#x201C;Time to Go&#x201D; alerts, which combine GPS and your calendar events to estimate time it&#x2019;ll take for you to travel from one place to another. Other notifications include text messages and email alerts from handpicked &#x201C;VIPs,&#x201D; to ensure that your wrist isn&#x2019;t constantly buzzing. Each function takes about two or three taps to enable.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;I get to decide who has the phone number here,&#x201D; Ildeniz said. &#x201C;I get to decide who are my VIPs: It&#x2019;s the close contact with my family and my loved ones.&#x201D;\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EYou can control the information that filters into the bracelet via an online portal, accessible via computer or smartphone. There you can change the background patterns of the device&#x2019;s display screen, load up your Gmail accounts, connect your Google and Facebook calendars, and log in to your Yelp account.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThough MICA does not connect or sync to your phone, it can be charged by your computer via a USB cord, and its battery life lasts up to two days, depending on the frequency of use. According to Humberto Leon, creative director and co-founder of Opening Ceremony, the two groups are collaborating on a bowl that charges the device as well.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"image\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F12b2979c77d7966b81a917acfcfbee130052ebae.jpg\"\u003E\u003Cem\u003E(Alyssa Bereznak\u002FYahoo Tech)\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe event, moderated by Lucky Magazine Editor-in-Chief Eva Chen, included a video advertisement featuring actress Rashida Jones and representatives from Intel, Opening Ceremony, and Barneys New York.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E&#x201C;Wearables and technology is still in its infancy,&#x201D; Ildeniz said. &#x201C;This is just one example of how we can actually expand the usage of wearables. It&#x2019;s going to be a much wider phenomenon when we come out with different devices that cater to different types of people. Today we&#x2019;re talking about a woman who wants to stay in touch with her loved ones. Tomorrow we could be talking about children. Gift Ideas: TV Streaming Sticks","summary":"No larger than your average USB thumb drive, streaming sticks like the Amazon Fire TV, Roku Stick, and Google’s Chromecast bring the Internet, and Internet video, to your HDTV.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Tech Gift Ideas: TV Streaming Sticks\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F45b54c93e692d83b8876a2352a9dbf3e1813d681.jpg\"\u003EIf you&#x2019;re looking for a stocking stuffer for the Comcast-hating cord cutter in your life, look no further than the fresh crop of TV streaming sticks.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ENo larger than your average USB thumb drive, streaming sticks like the Amazon Fire TV, Roku Stick, and Google&#x2019;s Chromecast connect to your home Wi-Fi network and plug into your television&#x2019;s HDMI port. Once configured, they let your TV-addicted loved ones stream their favorite shows, apps, and movies on the boob tube, using a variety of both free and paid Internet services.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EEach of these streaming sticks is priced south of $50, less expensive than streaming boxes like the Roku&#xA0;3 or Apple TV. For that price, you&#x2019;re going to sacrifice some power and, occasionally, a remote control. But each of the sticks we&#x2019;re about to offer gets the job done, at the very least bringing Netflix and YouTube to your television.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe question is: Which one of these sticks should find its way into your favorite person&#x2019;s stocking this year?\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ERoku Streaming Stick (HDMI version): $49\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ERoku is synonymous with media streaming boxes, thanks to the company&#x2019;s set-top boxes. The most expensive Roku box, the Roku&#xA0;3, costs $100. So it&#x2019;s the \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.roku.com\u002Fproducts\u002Fstreaming-stick\"\u003ERoku Streaming Stick\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E that is perhaps the most compelling low-cost gift idea for TV and movie fanatics.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe Roku Stick gets the same 1,500-plus apps available for the Roku&#xA0;3 set-top box with the same interface, at half the price. And like the Roku&#xA0;3, the Roku Stick gets a traditional remote with customizable shortcut buttons for your favorite apps.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Roku streaming stick\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F76a3cdb28b4b294bef2e4154ae6bab4f35473a7c.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EYou can also cast video from apps like Netflix and YouTube from your smartphone or tablet directly to the Roku Stick and onto your TV. And if you lose the included remote control, you can also use your smartphone as a remote for the Stick, using the Roku app.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThere are some drawbacks to the Roku Stick, though. Because its guts are packed into such a small body, the Roku Stick isn&#x2019;t as powerful as its set-top box sibling the Roku&#xA0;3. As a result, some apps might take longer to open. The Stick also uses a separate USB cable for power, so there might be some additional cord clutter behind your boob tube.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EStill, for just under $50 you get one of the best media streaming devices around.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EBuy it for:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E The TV and movie junkie who wants every streaming service and a simple-to-use device.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fyahooshopping.pgpartner.com\u002Fplr.php?id=8016\"\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003ECheck price.\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EAmazon Fire TV Stick: $39\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ELike the Roku Stick, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.amazon.com\u002Fdp\u002FB00GDQ0RMG\u002Fref=nav_shopall_k_tv_stick\"\u003EAmazon&#x2019;s Fire TV Stick\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, which is available for preorder, is a scaled-down version of its set-top cousin, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.yahoo.com\u002Ftech\u002Famazon-unveils-fire-tv-a-streaming-media-box-to-rival-81491042043.html\"\u003Ethe Fire TV\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E, but at a fraction of the price. The Fire TV Stick plugs into the back of your TV via its HDMI port. As with the Roku Stick, though, it also needs an outside power source, so you&#x2019;ll have to have a free power outlet nearby.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EOn the plus side, the Fire TV Stick gives you access to all the same great features as the Fire TV (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=HHoNQrxG_8M\"\u003EGary Busey&#x2019;s teeth not included\u003C\u002Fa\u003E). So your favorite person will be able to stream \u003Cem\u003ELeprechaun\u003C\u002Fem\u003E on Netflix, watch \u003Cem\u003EBob&#x2019;s Burgers\u003C\u002Fem\u003E on Hulu Plus, and catch up on episodes of \u003Cem\u003EThe Americans\u003C\u002Fem\u003E through Amazon Prime.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"Fire TV stick\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002Fa3ca003315d3f1b5dd8ba80d0518f87a1587707b.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThere are also a good number of casual games available for the Fire TV Stick, including \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003ETetris \u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003Eand \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Cem\u003EFlappy Bird\u003C\u002Fem\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ESo what&#x2019;s the downside to the Fire TV Stick? Well, unlike the Fire TV box, the Stick&#x2019;s remote doesn&#x2019;t support voice search. So you can&#x2019;t do things like name an actor and have the Fire TV Stick pull up all the movies he&#x2019;s been in that you can watch. Instead, you have to either buy the remote separately or download the Fire&#x2019;s smartphone app.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOh, and like the Fire TV, the Fire TV Stick doesn&#x2019;t have access to HBO GO. So if you&#x2019;re shopping for a \u003Cem\u003EGame of Thrones\u003C\u002Fem\u003E fan, you might want to think twice about Amazon&#x2019;s stick.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EBuy it for: \u003C\u002Fstrong\u003EThe Amazon Prime member who wants quick access to her Prime movies, Netflix, and Hulu, and doesn&#x2019;t mind missing out on HBO GO.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fyahooshopping.pgpartner.com\u002Fplr.php?id=8006\"\u003ECheck price.\u003C\u002Fa\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EGoogle Chromecast: $35\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThe least expensive of the bunch, \u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.google.com\u002Fchrome\u002Fdevices\u002Fchromecast\u002F#cc-video\"\u003EGoogle&#x2019;s Chromecast\u003C\u002Fa\u003E,\u003Cspan\u003E is also the oldest streaming stick in this group. As with the Roku Stick and Fire TV Stick, Chromecast connects to your TV via an HDMI port and uses an available USB port for power.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThere are, however, some major differences between Google&#x2019;s offering and its competitors. First off, Chromecast doesn&#x2019;t have a traditional home screen from which you can choose apps or videos to watch.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003E\u003Cimg alt=\"TV and smartphone displaying Chromecast app\" src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fg\u002Fimages\u002Fspaceball.gif\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fs.yimg.com\u002Fcd\u002Fresizer\u002F2.0\u002FFIT_TO_WIDTH-w500\u002F1287c0424c0d85c8f2f7979507e61509b687c982.jpg\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EInstead, Chromecast relies on you to download compatible apps to your smartphone or tablet. You then open what you want to play in that app and press the Cast button at the top of the app to send your video from your device to Chromecast and your TV.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003ESo, for example, you might download the Netflix app to your iPhone, and then find your movie there. Once the movie starts, the Cast icon will appear. You press it, and the movie switches from your phone to the television. And, yes, you can use your phone for other things while the movie plays on the TV set.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EOn the plus side, you&#x2019;re not limited to just using the smartphone or tablet, as you can also cast things from your Chrome browser for Windows or Mac, or from your Chromebook.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EHere&#x2019;s the thing, though. Chromecast doesn&#x2019;t come with a remote, but instead relies on your connected smartphone or tablet, which can be a bummer when you go to skip the next episode of \u003Cem\u003EMad Men\u003C\u002Fem\u003E and instead see a notification from the boss on your phone.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cspan\u003EThat being said, the Chromecast&#x2019;s price can&#x2019;t be beat, and its flexibility is impressive.\u003C\u002Fspan\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cstrong\u003EBuy it for:\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E The Google and Android fanatic who also wants to be able to view websites, and video from websites, on his television.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ca Will Now Let You Stream Your Favorite Spotify Playlists During Rides","summary":"Uber’s big music-related announcement is indeed a new partnership with Spotify.  Starting Nov. 21, riders will be able to choose their own playlists that’ll stream as they ride to their destinations.","body":"\u003Cp\u003E\u003Ciframe height=\"281.25\" width=\"500\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fembed\u002FtBY5Lbcc5wE\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EUber&#x2019;s big music-related announcement is indeed&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2014\u002F11\u002F15\u002F7225167\u002Fuber-and-spotify-reportedly-partnering-to-bring-custom-playlists-to-rides\"\u003Ea new partnership with Spotify\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Starting Nov. 21, riders will be able to choose their own playlists that&#x2019;ll stream as they ride to their destinations. The Uber\u002FSpotify integration will be offered in 10 cities at launch: New York, San Francisco, Nashville, Los Angeles, London, Mexico City, Singapore, Stockholm, Toronto, and Sydney. It&#x2019;ll continue to roll out to new areas in the weeks and months to come. Essentially, you&#x2019;ll be able to hijack a driver&#x2019;s normal listening choices and play any song in Spotify&#x2019;s giant catalog.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \n\u003Cp\u003EThe process involves linking your Spotify and Uber accounts. (A premium Spotify subscription is required.) Once you do that and choose a playlist from within the Uber app, a driver can have your favorite tracks playing before you even get into the car. Or maybe you don&#x2019;t mind letting your driver&#xA0;\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=h-vwPuiILBc\"\u003Elisten to his own jams\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Just remember: Uber passengers get rated too, so don&#x2019;t abuse your new-found Spotify privileges. And if drivers have zero interest in hearing your favorite playlists, they&#x2019;re not required to participate.
